⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرف. تعريف المعرف، وشروطه، وأقسامه. ما يُحد ويُحد به، وما لا يُحد ولا يُحد به. بعض الأبحاث المتعلقة بالحد. دفع شك الإمام الرازي أن التعريف تحصيل الحاصل. الاختلاف الواقع بين السيد والسعد في أن التعريف اللفظي هل هو من المطالب التصورية، أم من المطالب التصديقية. لا يتوجه على التعريف شيء من المُنوع، وأما ما تضمنه من الأحكام الضمنية فيجوز إيرادها عليه، إلا أن العلماء منع ذلك أيضا. يجوز نقض الحد بإبطال الطرد والعكس. تجري المعارضة في الحدود الحقيقية، دون الرسمية. اللفظ المفرد لا يدل على التفصيل، وما يترتب على ذلك من الأبحاث. القسم الثاني التصديقات. الفرق بين الحكم الإجمالي والحكم التفصيلي، والنسبة تدخل في متعلق الحكم. أجزاء القضية ثلاثة، وما يتعلق به من الأبحاث. وفي لغة العرب رابطة كغيرها من اللغات ولا حاجة إلى الاستعارة خلافا للسعد. ما يراه المحقق صوابا في هذه المسألة. تقسيم القضية إلى الحملية والشرطية. هل الحكم في الشرطية في الجزاء، أم باللزوم بين التالي والمقدم، وهل بين النحاة والمناطقة خلاف في ذلك؟ فصل، تقسيم القضية باعتبار الموضوع إلى شخصية ومهملة وطبيعية ومحصورة. المهملة تلازم الجزئية عند المتأخرين. اختيار قول الدواني إن الحكم في المحصورة على نفس الحقيقة، والجزئيات معلومة بالعرض. المحصورات أربع، وسور كل منها. تبصرة في تحقيق المحصورات. تعبيرهم عن الموضوع بـ (ج) وعن المحمول بـ(ب). الإطلاقات الثلاثة للفظ «الكل». المعتبر في العلوم من تلك الإطلاقات هو «الكل الأفرادي». المراد بـ(ج) هو ذات الموضوع، أي ما يصدق عليه الموضوع من الأفراد. الخلاف بين الفارابي وابن سينا في معنى صدق عنوان الموضوع على ذاته. عقد الوضع وعقد الحمل (المحقق).
Chapter on Definition. Definition of definition, its conditions, and its divisions. What is defined and what is defined by, and what is not defined nor defines by. Some investigations related to definition. Refutation of the doubt of Imam al-Razi that definition is the acquisition of what is already acquired. The disagreement between al-Sayyid and al-Sa'd regarding whether verbal definition is among conceptual demands or among assertive demands. Nothing from the objections applies to definition; as for what it includes of implicit judgments, it is permissible to object to them, except that the scholars also forbade that. It is permissible to refute the definition by invalidating the 'tard' and 'aks'. Objection is valid against real definitions, not against descriptive ones. The single word does not indicate detail, and the investigations resulting from that. The second section: Assents. The difference between total judgment and detailed judgment, and the relation enters into the object of judgment. The parts of a proposition are three, and the investigations related to it. In the language of the Arabs, there is a copula like other languages, and there is no need for metaphor, contrary to al-Sa'd. What the investigator deems correct in this issue. Division of proposition into categorical and conditional. Is the judgment in the conditional upon the consequent, or upon the implication between the consequent and antecedent? Is there a disagreement between grammarians and logicians on that? Chapter: Division of proposition with respect to subject into individual, indefinite, natural, and quantified. The indefinite implies the particular according to the later scholars. Choosing the view of al-Dawani that the judgment in a quantified proposition is upon the essence itself, and the particulars are known accidentally. The quantified propositions are four, and the quantifier of each. Insight into the verification of quantified propositions. Their expression of the subject by (J) and of the predicate by (B). The three usages of the word 'all'. What is considered in sciences among those usages is 'the individual all'. What is meant by (J) is the essence of the subject, i.e., what the subject applies to of individuals. The disagreement between al-Farabi and Ibn Sina on the meaning of the predicate of the subject's title upon itself. The contract of subject and contract of predicate (al-Muhaqqiq).
Source pages p. 627

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents for the treatise 'Bahr Ulum' on Islamic logic. It outlines the major sections, starting with definitions and their conditions, then moves to the second major section on assents (tasdiqat). Under definitions, the author discusses the refutation of al-Razi's doubt, the disagreement on verbal definition, and the permissibility of objections. For assents, the table covers the parts of a proposition, the copula debate, the division of propositions into categorical and conditional, and the division by subject type. It also notes controversies among later scholars such as al-Dawani, al-Sayyid, and al-Sa'd, and references disagreements between al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. This table serves as a roadmap, showing the logical flow from conceptual to assertive matters, with focus on definition, proposition structure, and quantified propositions.

القضية
المحمول

Checkpoint
According to the author, does Arabic have a copula?
A) Yes, like other languages
B) No, it must borrow
C) It has only in conditional sentences
D) The copula is not needed for logical analysis

Key Takeaway
The structure of propositions in Arabic is parallel to other languages; recognizing the copula helps in formal logical analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take an Arabic nominal sentence like 'الكتاب مفيد' (The book is useful). Identify its three parts and state the copula (explicit or implicit). Then explain whether you agree with the author or al-Sa'd.
?
Construct a categorical syllogism using two Arabic propositions with implicit copulas, and show the copula explicitly in your analysis.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Quantified Propositions and Symbols (J) and (B)
Symbols for subject and predicate in quantified propositions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret the symbols (J) and (B) in quantified propositions and recall the four quantifiers.

Core Idea
(J) stands for the subject, (B) for the predicate, streamlining logical notation.

The table introduces the symbols for subject and predicate, along with the four quantified propositions. This lesson explains how (J) and (B) are used and the meaning of 'all' in scientific contexts.

Guided Path
1
Note the four quantified propositions
The passage says 'المحصورات أربع' – there are four quantified propositions. These are universal affirmative, universal negative, particular affirmative, particular negative.
Each has a specific quantifier (sawr).
2
Understand the symbols
Find 'تعبيرهم عن الموضوع بـ (ج) وعن المحمول بـ(ب)' – they express the subject by (J) and the predicate by (B).
These are Arabic letter symbols: ج for mawdu', ب for mahmul.
3
Distinguish the three usages of 'all'
The passage mentions 'الإطلاقات الثلاثة للفظ «الكل»' – three usages of 'all' (kull). The 'individual all' is the relevant one in sciences.
This avoids ambiguity in universal statements.
4
Recognize the Farabi-Ibn Sina disagreement
There is a disagreement 'بين الفارابي وابن سينا في معنى صدق عنوان الموضوع على ذاته' – about whether the predicate applies to the subject's essence or to its individuals.
This affects interpretation of quantified propositions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Table of Contents of a Mantiq Text
Lists chapter and section headings for topics on propositions, syllogisms, and logical theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate any major topic in the Bahr al-Ulum commentary on Sullum al-Ulum using the table of contents.

Core Idea
The fihris is a treasure map for the logical journey.

The table of contents is more than a list; it's a structural outline of the arguments ahead. This lesson will train you to read it as a map of the logical terrain, so you can efficiently find discussions on propositions, their divisions, and modal logic.

Guided Path
1
Scan the major divisions
Notice the progression: first propositions (القضية), then division into categorical (الحملية) and conditional (الشرطية), then modal propositions (الموجهات), and finally conditionals again. This mirrors the logical order of study.
2
Identify page numbers
Each heading has a page number (given in Arabic numerals). Use these to quickly navigate. Some numbers are misaligned in this OCR, so verify when reading the actual book.
Page numbers like 362, 363, 373, etc. are listed vertically.
3
Note sub-sections
Under each heading, look for sub-topics. For example, under 'تقسيم القضية إلى الحملية والشرطية', there follow questions about the nature of judgment in conditionals and disagreements between grammarians and logicians.
4
Key terms as structural markers
The table introduces important terms like 'المحصورات' (quantified propositions) and 'الشرطية المنفصلة' (disjunctive conditionals). Notice where they appear to anticipate their full discussion later.
Terms like 'ج' and 'ب' are introduced as notation.

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents for the Bahr Ulum commentary on the Sullum al-Ulum. It lists chapter and section headings covering logical propositions and their divisions. The topics progress from the parts of a proposition, the copula in Arabic, division into categorical and conditional, then division by subject type into individual, neglected, natural, and quantified. Later sections cover modal propositions and conditionals. The table serves as a navigational tool, and the student should use it to understand the book's structure. Logical variables ج and ب are mentioned as standard notation for subject and predicate. The page numbers are given in Arabic numerals, though some may be misaligned in this OCR.
